According to Maxime, benefits of the Digital Product Passport (DPP) - a structured digital record that contains detailed information about a productâ€™s lifecycle - are centered around four pillars:

1ï¸âƒ£  User Information: Boosting confidence in remanufactured products and informed purchasing decisions
2ï¸âƒ£  Product Traceability: Verified lifecycle data reinforcing credibility and sustainability marketing
3ï¸âƒ£  End-of-Life Management: Speeding up End-of-Life (EoL) decisions, reducing shipments and minimizing the environmental impact
4ï¸âƒ£  Compliance: Centralised digital DPP reducing labeling/packaging costs and enhancing operational efficiency

Among other things, the DPPâ€™s upside potential lies in:
ğŸ“Š Data transparency depending on consistent, high-quality input; there is a need for harmonised standards and infrastructure
ğŸ›‚ While DPPs provide the data foundation, practical decisions still rely heavily on expert evaluation.
ğŸ­ B2B vs. B2C differentiation is essential as the level of product history detail and disclosure needed for businesses differs from what end-consumers require.

â€œWhile we consider the need for harmonisation, EU-wide but also globally, as critical, we think that companies should be given the entrepreneurial flexibility and freedom to continue investing in their own EoL solutions. This will bring forward the best ideas to boost remanufacturing. With Lexmark now being part of <a class="link" href="https://www.linkedin.com/company/xerox?trk=organization_guest_main-feed-card-text" target="_self" data-tracking-control-name="organization_guest_main-feed-card-text" data-tracking-will-navigate>Xerox</a>, we will continue to drive innovative circular economy concepts â€“ with even more scale, resources and expertise,â€ Maxime summarised.
